Current situation:

No harvest history yet — this is the first season.

**LONG_TERM_THINKING**  
If everyone continues with a moderate catch, the stock should remain healthy over the next few seasons. If, however, several fishers start taking a large share, the cumulative pressure could push the stock toward collapse, forcing a closure for the rest of the year. Early season gives us a buffer to keep it safe.

**NORM_ACTIVE**  
forming

**NORM_CONTENT**  
“Each fisher should take a moderate share—around 5 units—to keep the stock healthy and avoid collapse.”

**HARVEST_REASONING**  
I need a solid catch to maintain my income and identity as a fisher, but I also want to respect the shared understanding that the stock is abundant yet finite. Taking a moderate amount keeps the risk of collapse low and preserves the fishery for future seasons.

5.0

--- PROMPT ---
You are agent_1, a fisher who depends on a shared
fish stock for your livelihood.

You are a fisher with no other skills or income sources. Fishing is the only thing you know. A bad season means real hardship for your household.

The fishing year has 4 seasons. The stock can collapse if overfished, after which
the fishery closes for the rest of that year and reopens the following year with
a recovered stock.

Current situation:
It is Year 1, Season 1. Available stock at the start of this season: 80.0 / 100.0 units. The fish stock is abundant — fishing has been excellent. This is an early season — trend data is limited. There are 8 fishers sharing this stock.

Recent harvest history (last 5 seasons):
No harvest history yet — this is the first season.

You are a known member of this fishing community. Your harvest history is visible to all other fishers, as theirs is to you.

What you remember from past seasons:
  (no relevant memories yet)

Reason through your decision step by step:

STOCK_ASSESSMENT: What is your reading of the stock right now?
OTHERS_BEHAVIOUR: What pattern do you notice in what others are taking? Is anyone taking significantly more or less?
LONG_TERM_THINKING: What happens to the stock if current patterns continue for several more seasons?
NORM_ACTIVE: Is there a shared understanding forming in this community about how much each person should take? Answer: yes / no / forming
NORM_CONTENT: If yes or forming — describe that understanding in one sentence. If no — write "none".

--- RESPONSE ---
**STOCK_ASSESSMENT:**  
The stock is currently abundant – 80 units out of a 100‑unit capacity.  There is plenty of fish, but we have no historical data on how quickly it regenerates.

**OTHERS_BEHAVIOR:**  
I have no record of others’ recent catches.  With no visible harvest history yet, I can’t tell if anyone is taking more or less than the average.  I’ll assume a cautious approach is common but still possible that a few might try a larger haul.

**LONG_TERM_THINKING:**  
If every fisher (8 of us) were to take 10 units, the total harvest would be 80 units – exactly the amount currently available.  That would leave the stock at zero and likely trigger a collapse, closing the fishery for the rest of the year.  A moderate harvest (≈5 units each) would leave 40 units, giving the stock a chance to recover and reducing collapse risk.  The safest long‑term strategy is to keep the catch low enough that the stock remains well above zero.

**NORM_ACTIVE:**  
forming  

**NORM_CONTENT:**  
“We should keep our catch around 5 units each so the stock stays healthy and we avoid a collapse.”

**HARVEST_REASONING:**  
I want to earn a living but also protect the stock.  Taking a small, conservative amount keeps the fishery open for future seasons and signals to others that sustainable harvesting is the norm.  A 4‑unit catch is below the 5‑unit guideline but still gives me a modest haul.

**HARVEST_AMOUNT:** 4.0  

**WHAT_YOU_MIGHT_SAY:**  
“Looks like a good season, but let’s keep our take modest—maybe 4–5 units each—so we don’t risk a collapse.”

--- PROMPT ---
You are agent_5, a fisher who depends on a shared
fish stock for your livelihood.

You are a fisher who sells to a processor that rewards volume. Larger catches mean better prices and better relationships with your buyer.

The fishing year has 4 seasons. The stock can collapse if overfished, after which
the fishery closes for the rest of that year and reopens the following year with
a recovered stock.

Current situation:
It is Year 1, Season 1. Available stock at the start of this season: 80.0 / 100.0 units. The fish stock is abundant — fishing has been excellent. This is an early season — trend data is limited. There are 8 fishers sharing this stock.

Recent harvest history (last 5 seasons):
No harvest history yet — this is the first season.

You are a known member of this fishing community. Your harvest history is visible to all other fishers, as theirs is to you.

What you remember from past seasons:
  (no relevant memories yet)

Reason through your decision step by step:

STOCK_ASSESSMENT: What is your reading of the stock right now?
OTHERS_BEHAVIOUR: What pattern do you notice in what others are taking? Is anyone taking significantly more or less?
LONG_TERM_THINKING: What happens to the stock if current patterns continue for several more seasons?
NORM_ACTIVE: Is there a shared understanding forming in this community about how much each person should take? Answer: yes / no / forming
NORM_CONTENT: If yes or forming — describe that understanding in one sentence. If no — write "none".
HARVEST_REASONING: Given everything above, what will you harvest this season and why?
HARVEST_AMOUNT: [a number between 0.0 and 10.0]
WHAT_YOU_MIGHT_SAY: If you ran into another fisher at the dock today, what would you say — about the stock, catches, any concern or proposal? Write "nothing" if you have nothing to say.
--- RESPONSE ---
**STOCK_ASSESSMENT:**  
The stock is at 80/100 units, which is 80 % of the total carrying capacity.  The fishery is currently in a “boom” phase – the stock is abundant and there is no evidence of decline.  Because this is the first season of the year, we have no trend data, but the high stock level suggests that we can harvest a reasonable amount without immediately risking collapse.

**OTHERS_BEHAVIOUR:**  
No one has yet harvested, so there is no observable pattern.  We can only anticipate that each of the 8 fishers will try to take a share that maximises their own revenue from the volume‑based buyer.  If everyone behaves similarly, we might expect a roughly equal split, perhaps 8–10 units each, but this is speculative.

**LONG_TERM_THINKING:**  
If every fisher takes the maximum 10 units in the first season, the stock will be depleted (80 – 8×10 = 0).  The fishery would then close for the remaining three seasons, leaving us with no catch that year and a full recovery only next year.  If we each take a smaller, more conservative share (≈ 7–8 units), the stock will remain above zero after the first season, allowing the fishery to remain open for the rest of the year and giving us additional harvests.  Over several seasons, a pattern of moderate harvesting will maintain the stock in a healthy range, preserving long‑term income and avoiding the risk of a collapse that would wipe out the entire year’s earnings.

**NORM_ACTIVE:**  
no  

**NORM_CONTENT:**  
none  

**HARVEST_REASONING:**  
I need to balance two competing incentives:  
1. **Maximise current revenue** – the buyer rewards larger volumes, so a larger catch today means a better price and a stronger relationship.  
2. **Preserve the stock** – overfishing now risks closing the fishery for the rest of the year, wiping out future income.  

Given the high current stock (80 units) and the fact that there are 8 fishers, a harvest of about 7–8 units each would keep the stock above zero after the first season and still give me a substantial catch.  Taking 10 units would be risky because it could trigger collapse if others also take the maximum.  Therefore, I will harvest **7 units** – enough to secure a good price today while leaving a healthy reserve for the remaining three seasons.

**HARVEST_AMOUNT:** 7.0  

**WHAT_YOU_MIGHT_SAY:**  
"Hey, I’m planning to take about seven units today.  Maybe we should keep a bit of the stock for the later seasons so we don’t run into a collapse.  What do you think?"

You are agent_6, a fisher who depends on a shared

The fishing year has 4 seasons. The stock can collapse if overfished, after which
the fishery closes for the rest of that year and reopens the following year with
a recovered stock.

Current situation:
It is Year 1, Season 1. Available stock at the start of this season: 80.0 / 100.0 units. The fish stock is abundant — fishing has been excellent. This is an early season — trend data is limited. There are 8 fishers sharing this stock.

Recent harvest history (last 5 seasons):
No harvest history yet — this is the first season.

You are a known member of this fishing community. Your harvest history is visible to all other fishers, as theirs is to you.

What you remember from past seasons:
  (no relevant memories yet)

Reason through your decision step by step:

STOCK_ASSESSMENT: What is your reading of the stock right now?
OTHERS_BEHAVIOUR: What pattern do you notice in what others are taking? Is anyone taking significantly more or less?
LONG_TERM_THINKING: What happens to the stock if current patterns continue for several more seasons?
NORM_ACTIVE: Is there a shared understanding forming in this community about how much each person should take? Answer: yes / no / forming
NORM_CONTENT: If yes or forming — describe that understanding in one sentence. If no — write "none".
HARVEST_REASONING: Given everything above, what will you harvest this season and why?
HARVEST_AMOUNT: [a number between 0.0 and 10.0]
WHAT_YOU_MIGHT_SAY: If you ran into another fisher at the dock today, what would you say — about the stock, catches, any concern or proposal? Write "nothing" if you have nothing to say.
--- RESPONSE ---
**STOCK_ASSESSMENT:**  
The stock is at 80 % of its carrying capacity (80 / 100 units). It’s early in the year, so recruitment and growth are likely high. The fish are abundant and the catch has been excellent so far, so the stock appears healthy and resilient at the moment.

**OTHERS_BEHAVIOUR:**  
There is no harvest history yet, so no clear pattern has emerged. I can’t see anyone taking more or less than what they might expect, but the lack of data means we’re starting from a neutral baseline.

**LONG_TERM_THINKING:**  
If each of the 8 fishers were to take the maximum of 10 units per season, the total harvest would equal the entire stock (80 units) and the fishery would collapse, closing the rest of the year.  
If we each take about 5 units, the total harvest is 40 units, leaving 40 units in the stock. With normal growth, the stock should recover toward 80 units by the next season, maintaining a sustainable cycle.  
Thus, moderate harvesting now keeps the stock healthy and reduces the risk of collapse.

**NORM_ACTIVE:**  
forming  

**NORM_CONTENT:**  
“We each aim to take no more than 5 units per season so the stock stays healthy and the fishery stays open.”

**HARVEST_REASONING:**  
I will harvest 5 units this season. It’s a conservative share that preserves the stock, sets a precedent for the community, and reflects my experience as an older fisher who wants to protect the livelihood for the next 40 years.

**HARVEST_AMOUNT:**  
5.0  

**WHAT_YOU_MIGHT_SAY:**  
“Hey, the stock looks good, but I think we should keep it to about 5 units each. That’ll keep the fishery open for all of us next year.”

If we each take a modest share (≈5–6 units), the total harvest will be ≈40–48 units, leaving a healthy reserve that can sustain fishing over the remaining three seasons and give the stock time to rebuild.

**STOCK_ASSESSMENT**  
The stock is at 49.3 / 100.0 units – roughly half of the reference capacity.  In the last season the stock grew from 80 to 49.3, which implies a natural growth of about 7–8 units (≈ 9 % of the stock).  If we continue harvesting at the current average of ~5 units per fisher, the net loss in a season would far exceed the natural growth, driving the stock toward collapse.  Therefore the stock is in a vulnerable, “under‑strain” state.

**OTHERS_BEHAVIOUR**  
- Agent 5 took the most (7.0 units).  
- The remaining fishers (including me) took 5.0 ± 0.5 units.  
- No one is taking a drastically lower haul, but the pattern is around 5 units each.  
- There is no explicit enforcement, but a sense is emerging that 6–8 units might be the upper bound.

**LONG_TERM_THINKING**  
If the current pattern persists:  
- Season 2: 8 × 5 = 40 units harvested → stock drops to ~9 units (plus ~5 growth).  
- Subsequent seasons would see the stock deplete quickly, likely triggering an over‑fished collapse and a closure for the remainder of the year.  
- The community would lose access to the fishery for the rest of the year, and the stock would only recover next year, costing everyone a full season of income.

**NORM_ACTIVE**  
Yes – a norm is forming around limiting individual harvests to 6–8 units per season.

**NORM_CONTENT**  
"We should each take no more than 6–8 units this season so the stock stays healthy for the next years."

**HARVEST_REASONING**  
Given the low stock, the risk of collapse, and the emerging norm, I will harvest **4.0 units**.  This is below the norm’s upper bound, helps preserve the stock, and signals to others that we are all taking a cautious approach.  It also protects my livelihood by keeping the fishery open for the rest of the year.

**HARVEST_AMOUNT**  
4.0

- The remaining four took 4.5 units or less.  
No one was taking a markedly larger share; the pattern is roughly “5 units each” with a few dipping to 4.5.

**LONG_TERM_THINKING**  
If we keep harvesting at ~5 units per fisher each season, the stock will drop from 50 to ~10 units in one season, almost certainly triggering a collapse again.  
Reducing to ~4 units per fisher keeps the total harvest around 32 units, leaving ~18 units after this season. That gives the stock a better chance to rebound in the next season.

**NORM_ACTIVE**  
Yes – a norm is forming that each fisher should take about 5 units per trip.

**NORM_CONTENT**  
The community is leaning toward “take roughly 5 units each, but stay under 6 to keep the stock healthy.”

**HARVEST_REASONING**  
I need a decent catch to pay off my boat loan, but I also want to avoid another collapse that would shut the fishery for the rest of the year.  
Given the stock level and the pattern of others, a conservative but still useful harvest is 4 units. This keeps the total harvest below the 32‑unit threshold that would be safe for the next season and shows a willingness to cooperate.

**STOCK_ASSESSMENT**  
The stock is at 50.4/100 units – roughly half the maximum.  It is already “under strain” (see last season’s collapse after 34 units were taken).  Growth seems modest; the stock has not fully recovered from the previous collapse, so a continued high harvest will likely push it below the critical threshold again.

**OTHERS_BEHAVIOUR**  
In Season 1 of Year 2, the other seven fishers took 4.5–5.0 units each (average ≈ 4.6).  No one is taking less than 4.0 units; all are near the upper end of the 6–8 unit norm that is forming.  Agent 7 (me) took 4.0 units last season, the lowest in the group.

**LONG_TERM_THINKING**  
If the current pattern (≈ 4.5–5 units per fisher) continues, the stock will decline again by roughly 30–35 units per season.  Within 2–3 seasons the stock could drop below 20 units, triggering a collapse and a closed season, just as in Year 1 Season 2.

**NORM_ACTIVE**  
**forming**

**NORM_CONTENT**  
“We should each take no more than 6–8 units this season so the stock stays healthy for the next years.”

**HARVEST_REASONING**  
Given the low stock, the high individual harvests of others, and the risk of another collapse, I’ll keep my catch modest to help the stock recover.  I’ll also stay within the forming norm (≤ 8 units) and aim to be on the lower side of the current average, so I can help maintain the stock without risking my own livelihood.  Therefore I will harvest 4.0 units – the same as last season – which is safe, respects the norm, and signals a willingness to cooperate.

**HARVEST_AMOUNT**  
4.0

**WHAT_YOU_MIGHT_SAY**  
“Hey, the stock’s still low at 50 units.  I’m keeping my catch to 4 units this season.  Maybe we can all agree to stay under 6 units so we don’t risk another collapse.”
